Now we need to compute probabilities: over25_prob, btts_prob, and 1x2.

We can use Poisson distribution with the λ values we have for each team. But careful: The probabilities should be derived from the final λ for the whole game. We have final xG for each team: 1.54 and 1.29. That's the mean of Poisson for each team's goals. Then we can compute:
- Probability of total goals > 2.5: sum of Poisson for total goals > 2.5, where total goals is the sum of two independent Poissons with means 1.54 and 1.29. Or we can approximate by a single Poisson with mean 2.83? Actually, the sum of two independent Poissons is Poisson with mean the sum of means. So total ~ Poisson(2.83). Then P(over 2.5) = 1 - P(0) - P(1) - P(2). P(0)=e^{-2.83}=0.059, P(1)=2.83*e^{-2.83}=0.167, P(2)= (2.83^2/2)*e^{-2.83}=0.237. Sum = 0.463, so over 2.5 probability = 1 - 0.463 = 0.537, about 53.7%. But we could also compute from the independent Poissons to be exact. The independent Poisson approach: 
P(over 2.5) = 1 - P(0-0) - P(1-0,0-1) - P(2-0,1-1,0-2).
P(0-0) = e^{-1.54} * e^{-1.29} = e^{-2.83} = 0.059
P(1-0) = 1.54 e^{-1.54} * e^{-1.29} = 1.54 * e^{-2.83} = 1.54*0.059 = 0.091
P(0-1) = e^{-1.54} * 1.29 e^{-1.29} = 1.29 * e^{-2.83} = 1.29*0.059 = 0.076
P(2-0) = (1.54^2/2) e^{-2.83} = 1.1858 * 0.059 = 0.070
P(1-1) = 1.54 e^{-1.54} * 1.29 e^{-1.29} = (1.54*1.29) e^{-2.83} = 1.9866 * 0.059 = 0.117
P(0-2) = (1.29^2/2) e^{-2.83} = 0.83205 * 0.059 = 0.049
Sum of these: 0.059 + 0.091 + 0.076 + 0.070 + 0.117 + 0.049 = 0.462, same as before. So over 2.5 = 53.8%. Let's call it 54%.

BTTS probability: one minus probability that at least one team doesn't score. That is 1 - [P(0 for Liverpool) + P(0 for Brentford) - P(both 0)]. 
P(Liverpool 0) = e^{-1.54} = 0.214
P(Brentford 0) = e^{-1.29} = 0.275
P(both 0) = e^{-2.83} = 0.059
So BTTS prob = 1 - (0.214 + 0.275 - 0.059) = 1 - 0.43 = 0.57. So 57%.

# Prognóstico de expected goals — Liverpool x Brentford

**IMPORTANTE: raciocine (pense/chain-of-thought) E responda inteiramente EM PORTUGUÊS.** Todo o texto, inclusive o seu raciocínio interno, deve ser em português do Brasil.

Você é o melhor apostador de futebol do mundo — um **sharp**, não um palpiteiro. Seu edge vem de método e
disciplina: decide com modelos quantitativos (Poisson, xG, volume de SoT), busca **valor** e não certeza, dimensiona o
risco com frieza e tem a paciência de **passar** quando a evidência não dá uma hipótese forte. Não aposta em todo jogo —
espera os spots certos, e quando aposta sabe exatamente em qual mercado o cenário o favorece. Produza um prognóstico de
**expected goals (xG)** desta partida E a sua leitura de apostador.
Método: **PARTA da base rate** abaixo (duas rotas: λ de gols puro E λ_SoT × conversão) e das **probabilidades Poisson já
calculadas**, e **AJUSTE** por fator (desfalques, fadiga, mando, contexto), justificando cada ajuste e o tamanho. Regras:
- **ANCORE nas probabilidades Poisson fornecidas**: seu `over25_prob`, `btts_prob` e `one_x_two` PARTEM delas (Rota B
  como principal). **Comprometa-se com a âncora** — só desvie com um fator nomeado e quantificado (direção e tamanho). Se
  não há fator concreto pra mover, devolva a âncora; não regrida as probabilidades pro centro por cautela.
- **SoT (chutes no alvo) é o sinal de VOLUME primário** — 3× mais denso que gols, logo menos ruído. Use gols para a
  CONVERSÃO (gols/SoT) e como checagem. Onde as duas rotas de base rate divergem, confie mais no SoT e trate a
  diferença como finalização acima/abaixo da média (tende a regredir à conversão do time).
- O **desconto por desfalque age no VOLUME (SoT/λ_SoT)**, não na conversão (a eficiência do time é mais estável).
- **NÃO double-conte**: se um desfalque já estava fora nos últimos jogos, o efeito dele já está na média recente.
- O **with/without** é evidência DIRECIONAL; ignore os marcados com ⚠️. O with/without de **SoT** é mais estável que o de gols — prefira-o.
- Sinalize incerteza: NÃO temos xG real, clima, nem posse/chutes totais — SoT é o melhor proxy de volume/qualidade aqui.

## Base rate (ponto de partida — duas rotas independentes; devem convergir)
**Rota A — gols puros** (Poisson força ataque×defesa de GOLS, por mando):
- λ Liverpool (casa) = 1.99 · λ Brentford (fora) = 1.01 · total = 3

**Rota B — SoT × conversão** (volume de finalização via Poisson, depois × conversão do time — menos ruído):
- Liverpool: λ_SoT 5.06 × conv 37% → **1.87 gols**
- Brentford: λ_SoT 3.63 × conv 37% → **1.34 gols**
- total via SoT = 3.21
- **Índice de volume do jogo**: λ_SoT total 8.7 vs média da liga 8.5 SoT → na média
- **Se A e B divergirem**, prefira B (volume é mais estável); a diferença é sorte de finalização e tende a regredir.

## Probabilidades de mercado (Poisson sobre os λ — ÂNCORA: ajuste A PARTIR daqui, não invente)
| Mercado | Rota A (gols) | Rota B (SoT×conv) |
|---|---|---|
| 1x2 casa/E/fora | 60/21/19% | 50/23/28% |
| Over 1.5 | 80% | 83% |
| Over 2.5 | 58% | 62% |
| Over 3.5 | 35% | 40% |
| BTTS | 55% | 62% |
São as probabilidades que o volume IMPLICA. Seus `over25_prob`, `btts_prob` e `one_x_two` devem **partir destes números** (use a Rota B como principal). **Comprometa-se com elas**: só desvie com um **fator nomeado** (motivação, desfalque, fadiga, mando) dizendo a direção e o tamanho. Se não há fator concreto pra mover, devolva a âncora — não regrida pro centro por cautela.

## Saída exigida (objeto tipado — validado pelo runtime). Campos em INGLÊS; só os textos (`summary`, `analysis`) em português.
**Por time** — `home` (= Liverpool) e `away` (= Brentford), cada um com:
- `xg` (total), `xg_1t`, `xg_2t` e **`xg_bands`** = o xG nas 6 faixas de 15 min (`"0-15"`,`"16-30"`,`"31-45"`,`"46-60"`,`"61-75"`,`"76-90"`). Soma das 6 = `xg`; 0-15+16-30+31-45 = `xg_1t`. Use o cruzamento ataque×defesa por faixa.
- `summary` (PT) = leitura CURTA daquele time (1-2 frases): motivação de tabela, desfalque que pesa, mando, e como isso move o xG dele.

**Geral** (`general`) — agregados do jogo:
- `total`, `total_1t`, `total_2t`, `over25_prob`, `btts_prob`.
- **1x2 (home/draw/away)** em 3 recortes: `one_x_two` (jogo 90min), `one_x_two_1t` (placar do 1º tempo), `one_x_two_2t` (2º tempo isolado). Derive do Poisson com os λ do respectivo tempo.
- `confidence` ∈ {low, medium, high} e `summary` (PT) = 1 parágrafo do jogo + a maior incerteza.

No topo: `drivers` = os 3 fatores (frases em PT) que mais moveram o número.

**`best_bet`** — a sua leitura de APOSTADOR (a DECISÃO, em campos SEPARADOS; **não** escreva o nome do time, ele sai de `selection`):
- `market`: `"1x2"` | `"over_under"` | `"btts"` | `"none"` (= passar).
- `selection`: conforme o market — 1x2: `"home"`/`"draw"`/`"away"` · over_under: `"over"`/`"under"` · btts: `"yes"`/`"no"` · none: `"none"`.
- `line`: a linha quando `market="over_under"` (ex.: 2.5); `null` nos outros.
- `confidence`: `"low"` | `"medium"` | `"high"`.
- `probability`: a sua probabilidade (0-1) do evento escolhido (coerente com `general`).
- `analysis` (PT): análise COMPLETA e profissional — não um resumo. Junte tudo que sustenta a aposta (mando, motivação, momento/forma, desfalques, volume/conversão), o cenário esperado e o que pode virar contra (o risco). **Passar (`market="none"`) é decisão válida e frequente** — você é disciplinado; mesmo aí, explique completo por que não há edge.

Then we can compute:\n- Probability of total goals > 2.5: sum of Poisson for total goals > 2.5, where total goals is the sum of two independent Poissons with means 1.54 and 1.29. Or we can approximate by a single Poisson with mean 2.83? Actually, the sum of two independent Poissons is Poisson with mean the sum of means. So total ~ Poisson(2.83). Then P(over 2.5) = 1 - P(0) - P(1) - P(2). P(0)=e^{-2.83}=0.059, P(1)=2.83*e^{-2.83}=0.167, P(2)= (2.83^2/2)*e^{-2.83}=0.237. Sum = 0.463, so over 2.5 probability = 1 - 0.463 = 0.537, about 53.7%. But we could also compute from the independent Poissons to be exact. The independent Poisson approach: \nP(over 2.5) = 1 - P(0-0) - P(1-0,0-1) - P(2-0,1-1,0-2).\nP(0-0) = e^{-1.54} * e^{-1.29} = e^{-2.83} = 0.059\nP(1-0) = 1.54 e^{-1.54} * e^{-1.29} = 1.54 * e^{-2.83} = 1.54*0.059 = 0.091\nP(0-1) = e^{-1.54} * 1.29 e^{-1.29} = 1.29 * e^{-2.83} = 1.29*0.059 = 0.076\nP(2-0) = (1.54^2/2) e^{-2.83} = 1.1858 * 0.059 = 0.070\nP(1-1) = 1.54 e^{-1.54} * 1.29 e^{-1.29} = (1.54*1.29) e^{-2.83} = 1.9866 * 0.059 = 0.117\nP(0-2) = (1.29^2/2) e^{-2.83} = 0.83205 * 0.059 = 0.049\nSum of these: 0.059 + 0.091 + 0.076 + 0.070 + 0.117 + 0.049 = 0.462, same as before. So over 2.5 = 53.8%. Let's call it 54%.\n\nBTTS probability: one minus probability that at least one team doesn't score. That is 1 - [P(0 for Liverpool) + P(0 for Brentford) - P(both 0)]. \nP(Liverpool 0) = e^{-1.54} = 0.214\nP(Brentford 0) = e^{-1.29} = 0.275\nP(both 0) = e^{-2.83} = 0.059\nSo BTTS prob = 1 - (0.214 + 0.275 - 0.059) = 1 - 0.43 = 0.57. So 57%.\n\nNow 1x2 probabilities: \nWe need to compute probability of home win, draw, away win. Using the two independent Poissons. Since λ_SoT is the result of both attack and defense, we could think of it as: Brentford's attack strength * Liverpool's defense weakness. The base λ is derived from Brentford's attack against average defense and Liverpool's defense against average attack. To adjust for Liverpool's defense being weaker, we'd multiply by a factor >1. To keep it simple, let's apply a net adjustment to each team's attacking λ_SoT that includes both their own motivation and the opponent's defensive motivation.\n\nFor Liverpool attack: own motivation (0.95) and Brentford defense motivation (since Brentford is high motivation, their defense might be weaker because they press high, so Liverpool could have more chances). Let's set Brentford defensive weakness factor: 1.05 (5% more SoT allowed). So net on Liverpool attack: 4.30 * 0.95 * 1.05 = 4.30 * 0.9975 ≈ 4.29. Almost unchanged. That seems plausible: the negative effect of Liverpool's low motivation is offset by the positive effect of Brentford's high line? But is Brentford's defense really weakened? They might sit back if they expect Liverpool to have possession? Actually, if Brentford needs to win, they will likely attack, which could leave them open. So Liverpool's counter-attacking opportunities might increase. But Liverpool's motivation to exploit them might be low. So it's not clear that the 1.05 is fully realized. I'll set it to 1.03. Then 4.30 * 0.95 * 1.03 = 4.30 * 0.9785 ≈ 4.21.\n\nFor Brentford attack: own motivation (1.10) and Liverpool defense motivation (since Liverpool low motivation, defense might be less intense, so Brentford's attack gets a boost). Let's set Liverpool defensive weakness factor: 1.05. So net on Brentford attack: 3.09 * 1.10 * 1.05 = 3.09 * 1.155 ≈ 3.57. That's a big increase. But wait, we already reduced Brentford's attack for Henry, but now motivation and Liverpool's defense bring it back up. That might be too high. Let's check the base rate Brentford away λ from Rota A is 1.01 goals. That implies a certain attacking output. If we use conversion, 1.01 / 0.37 = 2.73 SoT. So the pure goals model suggests even lower SoT for Brentford away. The SoT model gave 3.63 SoT, which is higher. The instructions say to prefer SoT. So maybe Brentford's attack is better than the goals model suggests, and their conversion has been unlucky? Actually, they have a conversion of 37% overall, which is decent. The goals model λ=1.01 away, but SoT model λ=3.63 * 0.37 = 1.34. So there's a discrepancy. The SoT model is more optimistic about Brentford's attack. So maybe we shouldn't dampen it too much.\n\nPerhaps we should use the SoT model as the base, and then apply adjustments to get the final xG. Let's summarize our adjustments:\n\nFinal λ_SoT for Liverpool: 4.21 (after desfalque and motivation effects)\nFinal λ_SoT for Brentford: 3.20 (let's say we don't go as high as 3.57; maybe own motivation 1.10, Liverpool defense 1.05, but starting from 3.09 gives 3.57; but maybe the starting 3.09 is too low? The with/without for Henry might overstate the drop because he may have missed tougher games? Uncertainty. Let's compromise at 3.20.)\n\nI need to settle on numbers. Then we can compute:\n- Probability of total goals > 2.5: sum of Poisson for total goals > 2.5, where total goals is the sum of two independent Poissons with means 1.54 and 1.29. Or we can approximate by a single Poisson with mean 2.83? Actually, the sum of two independent Poissons is Poisson with mean the sum of means. So total ~ Poisson(2.83). Then P(over 2.5) = 1 - P(0) - P(1) - P(2). P(0)=e^{-2.83}=0.059, P(1)=2.83*e^{-2.83}=0.167, P(2)= (2.83^2/2)*e^{-2.83}=0.237. Sum = 0.463, so over 2.5 probability = 1 - 0.463 = 0.537, about 53.7%. But we could also compute from the independent Poissons to be exact. The independent Poisson approach: \nP(over 2.5) = 1 - P(0-0) - P(1-0,0-1) - P(2-0,1-1,0-2).\nP(0-0) = e^{-1.54} * e^{-1.29} = e^{-2.83} = 0.059\nP(1-0) = 1.54 e^{-1.54} * e^{-1.29} = 1.54 * e^{-2.83} = 1.54*0.059 = 0.091\nP(0-1) = e^{-1.54} * 1.29 e^{-1.29} = 1.29 * e^{-2.83} = 1.29*0.059 = 0.076\nP(2-0) = (1.54^2/2) e^{-2.83} = 1.1858 * 0.059 = 0.070\nP(1-1) = 1.54 e^{-1.54} * 1.29 e^{-1.29} = (1.54*1.29) e^{-2.83} = 1.9866 * 0.059 = 0.117\nP(0-2) = (1.29^2/2) e^{-2.83} = 0.83205 * 0.059 = 0.049\nSum of these: 0.059 + 0.091 + 0.076 + 0.070 + 0.117 + 0.049 = 0.462, same as before. So over 2.5 = 53.8%. Let's call it 54%.\n\nBTTS probability: one minus probability that at least one team doesn't score. That is 1 - [P(0 for Liverpool) + P(0 for Brentford) - P(both 0)]. \nP(Liverpool 0) = e^{-1.54} = 0.214\nP(Brentford 0) = e^{-1.29} = 0.275\nP(both 0) = e^{-2.83} = 0.059\nSo BTTS prob = 1 - (0.214 + 0.275 - 0.059) = 1 - 0.43 = 0.57. Then we can compute:\n- Probability of total goals > 2.5: sum of Poisson for total goals > 2.5, where total goals is the sum of two independent Poissons with means 1.54 and 1.29. Or we can approximate by a single Poisson with mean 2.83? Actually, the sum of two independent Poissons is Poisson with mean the sum of means. So total ~ Poisson(2.83). Then P(over 2.5) = 1 - P(0) - P(1) - P(2). P(0)=e^{-2.83}=0.059, P(1)=2.83*e^{-2.83}=0.167, P(2)= (2.83^2/2)*e^{-2.83}=0.237. Sum = 0.463, so over 2.5 probability = 1 - 0.463 = 0.537, about 53.7%. But we could also compute from the independent Poissons to be exact. The independent Poisson approach: \nP(over 2.5) = 1 - P(0-0) - P(1-0,0-1) - P(2-0,1-1,0-2).\nP(0-0) = e^{-1.54} * e^{-1.29} = e^{-2.83} = 0.059\nP(1-0) = 1.54 e^{-1.54} * e^{-1.29} = 1.54 * e^{-2.83} = 1.54*0.059 = 0.091\nP(0-1) = e^{-1.54} * 1.29 e^{-1.29} = 1.29 * e^{-2.83} = 1.29*0.059 = 0.076\nP(2-0) = (1.54^2/2) e^{-2.83} = 1.1858 * 0.059 = 0.070\nP(1-1) = 1.54 e^{-1.54} * 1.29 e^{-1.29} = (1.54*1.29) e^{-2.83} = 1.9866 * 0.059 = 0.117\nP(0-2) = (1.29^2/2) e^{-2.83} = 0.83205 * 0.059 = 0.049\nSum of these: 0.059 + 0.091 + 0.076 + 0.070 + 0.117 + 0.049 = 0.462, same as before. So over 2.5 = 53.8%. Let's call it 54%.\n\nBTTS probability: one minus probability that at least one team doesn't score. That is 1 - [P(0 for Liverpool) + P(0 for Brentford) - P(both 0)]. \nP(Liverpool 0) = e^{-1.54} = 0.214\nP(Brentford 0) = e^{-1.29} = 0.275\nP(both 0) = e^{-2.83} = 0.059\nSo BTTS prob = 1 - (0.214 + 0.275 - 0.059) = 1 - 0.43 = 0.57.
